        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer761470901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7749576475837424512"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*Not such a bad re-read*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote><br/><b>
  <u>Re-read: 05.06.2018</u>
</b><br/>I decided to re-read this book simply because I can't find anything new to read. Nothing interesting me anymore, and the sad part is that most of my re-reads are a complete bust. Luckily, this one actually wasn't so bad. <b>The story is really interesting and the characters are great</b>. The timeline is over months and I liked that; you get to know the characters, you get to <i>feel</i> and get to know the world, and you get action the whole way.</span>
  <span id="freeText7749576475837424512" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*Not such a bad re-read*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Re-read: 05.06.2018</u>
</b><br>I decided to re-read this book simply because I can't find anything new to read. Nothing interesting me anymore, and the sad part is that most of my re-reads are a complete bust. Luckily, this one actually wasn't so bad. <b>The story is really interesting and the characters are great</b>. The timeline is over months and I liked that; you get to know the characters, you get to <i>feel</i> and get to know the world, and you get action the whole way. The book is not focused on romance, but in healing, friendships, bravery and growth. I recommend everyone who liked high fantasy to read this series. <b>Overall, I'm glad I did the re-read</b>. The book has no slow spots, nor boring spots, things happen all the time, and it isn't incredibly predictable. I still like it.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Oh, you made an impression. Like a stone caught in my boot.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The book centers around <b>Avry of Kazan</b> (20), who is a healer; she absorbs their wounds and diseases into herself by laying hands upon the injured and dying. Healers like Avry are accused of spreading the plague that has decimated the Territories, leaving the survivors in a state of chaos. So instead of being appreciated, she gets hunted. Avry gets abducted by a band of rogues; must heal a plague-stricken prince, the leader of a campaign against her people, however, though Avry could heal their friend of the plague, she wouldn't then be able to heal myself. Would he be worth her life to save? <b>What they asked of her would be essentially trading one death—swift and certain—for another</b>—slow, painful and just as certain.. The story centers around their traveling to the daunting Nine Mountain, where they meet all kinds of danger mercenaries to magical dangers.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>The horrors from the dark years of the plague were still fresh in the survivors’ minds. They considered those times a war. A war that had been started by healers, who then spread the deadly disease, and refused to heal it.<br>Of course it was utter nonsense. We couldn’t heal the plague. And we didn’t start it. But in the midst of the chaos, no one listened to reason. Someone had to be blamed. Right?<br>The girl’s screams pierced my heart. I couldn’t stand it any longer. Three years on the run. Three years of hiding. Three terrible years full of fear and loneliness. For what? My life? Yes, I live and breathe and exist. Nothing else.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b><u>Other characters</u>:</b><br>↦ <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Prince <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <b>Kerrick of Alga</b> (26), leader of a band of rogues. He is a forest mage. His magic is a gift from the living essence of the forest. The Realm of Alga was north of the Nine Mountains.<br>↦ <b>Belen ‘Poppa Bear’ of Alga</b> (30), <b>Loren</b> (maybe 35), <b>Quain</b> (close to Avry's age), <b>Flea</b> (16), part of the band of rogues. Kerrick and Belen uses swords, Loren, an arrow notched in his bow, Quain, a nasty curved dagger and Flea, a switchblade. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jael kills Flea. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>↦ Prince <b>Ryne of Ivdel Realmm</b>, the one who’s sick and Kerrick wants Avry to heal.<br>↦ King <b>Tohon of Sogra</b> (25-26?), a life magician and he wants to be king of all fifteen Realms. Magic-wise, Tohon’s probably the most powerful mage living.<br>↦ <b>The High Priestess</b>, also known as <b>Estrid of Ozero</b> was intolerant of other faiths, and required her subjects to be members of her cultlike religion. She, Tohon and Ryne is battling for the rule?<br>↦ <b>Noelle of Kazan</b> (14), Avry's sister, hateful little girl.<br>↦ <b>Jael of Alga</b>, she and Kerrick were betrothed and almost to the altar when a stronger suitor stole her heart. She has air magic; it obeys her. She can even take your breath. Her mother-in-law is the High Priestess Estrid of Ozero. Jael married her oldest son, Stanslov of Ozero. He was first in line for the throne, but he left her a widow.<br>↦ <b>Inari</b> (looked to be about 13), in a bad situation and trying to survive, is forced to be a servant for the High Priestess’s family to avoid being sent to a training camp.<br>↦ <b>Sepp</b>, a death magician.<br>Cellina of Lyady (25-26?)<br>↦ <b>Danny</b> (12 and 3-quarters) and <b>Zila</b> (8), (maybe) made healers by Tohon by experiments. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The heart is a strange beast and not ruled by logic.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b><u>Quick basic facts</u>:</b><br><b>Genre</b>: - (Young Adult) High (?) Fantasy.<br><b>Series</b>: - Series, Book One.<br><b>Love triangle?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Cheating?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>HEA?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Favorite character?</b> - Kerrick of Alga.<br><b>Would I read more by this author/or of series?</b> - Yes.<br><b>Would I recommend this book/series?</b> - Yes.<br><b>Will I read this again in the future?</b> - Who knows. <br><b>New Rating</b> - 3/3.5 stars.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445268775i/16623124.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>First read: 26.11.13</u>
</b><br><b>Rate: 3/4 stars. </b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_215998779" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/215998779" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/215998779?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer215998779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7313080217821865897">2 1/2 stars<br/><br/>I am and will always be a huge fan of Maria V. Snyder’s first novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60510.Poison_Study__Study___1_' title='Poison Study (Study, #1) by Maria V. Snyder' rel='nofollow noopener'>Poison Study</a>. In fact, this is a little bit embarrassing but…I’ve read it <i>three times</i>. And I’m still not tired of it. <br/><br/>I’ve also read every single book that she’s published, but nothing has ever reached the level of that first love for me. I like the Glass series, but I don’t love it. The Inside/Out series is a cool sci-fi dystopian departure for her and I like it for that, but again...don’t love it. So when I saw tha</span>
  <span id="freeText7313080217821865897" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars<br /><br />I am and will always be a huge fan of Maria V. Snyder’s first novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60510.Poison_Study__Study___1_" title="Poison Study (Study, #1) by Maria V. Snyder" rel="nofollow noopener">Poison Study</a>. In fact, this is a little bit embarrassing but…I’ve read it <i>three times</i>. And I’m still not tired of it. <br /><br />I’ve also read every single book that she’s published, but nothing has ever reached the level of that first love for me. I like the Glass series, but I don’t love it. The Inside/Out series is a cool sci-fi dystopian departure for her and I like it for that, but again...don’t love it. So when I saw that the initial reviews for this one were positive, I couldn’t have been more excited to read it. <br /> <br />Unfortunately, this is another case of “like but don’t love.” Except, I feel like this one is even more of a let-down, because it’s so similar to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60510.Poison_Study__Study___1_" title="Poison Study (Study, #1) by Maria V. Snyder" rel="nofollow noopener">Poison Study</a>. Avry is sentenced to die, but is “rescued” and asked to perform a job that may also lead to her death. She becomes part of a band of soldiers/men who train her in knife throwing and survival. The love interest is cold and calculating, and dedicated in service to a progressive leader. There’s even a scene where Avry must play hide and seek in the woods and camouflages herself with clay. Avry and Yelena also have a very similar voice, in my opinion.<br /><br />I do love the imaginative magic system; although, the healing is again similar to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60510.Poison_Study__Study___1_" title="Poison Study (Study, #1) by Maria V. Snyder" rel="nofollow noopener">Poison Study</a>. (Yelena also heals Opal by assuming her injuries.) I really like the history of the plague: how the grief of the populace, fueled by rumor, could turn to hatred of the healers. I love the feuding “boarding school for nobles” graduates. In fact I would say that the world-building is one of my favorite aspects of this book. But there’s not much else here.<br /><br />It’s like reading a version of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60510.Poison_Study__Study___1_" title="Poison Study (Study, #1) by Maria V. Snyder" rel="nofollow noopener">Poison Study</a> that’s been bleached of all nuance and drained of all emotion. A cold, matter of fact voice worked very well for damaged, solitary, and ruthlessly independent Yelena, but makes absolutely no sense for Avry, who’s a self-sacrificing, altruistic healer. I never felt anything past the very surface of emotion for these characters. I wasn’t affected at all when they triumphed, suffered, died, loved…. The romance is so completely dry. In many ways, this feels like the outline of a book: all the bare bones of story, action, and dialogue are there but little else.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />ABBA – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cvChjHcABPA&amp;ob=av2e" rel="nofollow noopener">S.O.S.</a><br /><br />I still have hope that this author can publish something that will reach me at the same level as Poison Study. But until then, all I have to say is…<br /><br /><i>What ever happened to our love? I wish I understood. It used to be so nice; it used to be so good.</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7313080217821865897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_239717505" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239717505" />
    <a title="Kogiopsis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis"><img alt="Kogiopsis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494267218p2/1462364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239717505?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kogiopsis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kogiopsis" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis">Kogiopsis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=galleys">galleys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=save-me-from-the-tropes">save-me-from-the-tropes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239717505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14637236589700602340">I'm definitely coming at this book from a different perspective than a lot of people I know, many of whom have read and loved at the very least Poison Study, and often more of Maria V. Snyder's books. This is my first by her and to be honest, I'm underwhelmed.<br/><br/>The concept is by far the strongest part of this book. Fifteen kingdoms, eleven types of magic, a land recovering from a deadly plague - glorious. While I have certain issues with the varieties of magic (they seem to almost-but-not-quite be</span>
  <span id="freeText14637236589700602340" style="display:none">I'm definitely coming at this book from a different perspective than a lot of people I know, many of whom have read and loved at the very least Poison Study, and often more of Maria V. Snyder's books. This is my first by her and to be honest, I'm underwhelmed.<br /><br />The concept is by far the strongest part of this book. Fifteen kingdoms, eleven types of magic, a land recovering from a deadly plague - glorious. While I have certain issues with the varieties of magic (they seem to almost-but-not-quite be elemental, and moon/sun magic sounds basically useless), I like that there were so many different types, and that within them there seemed to be some variation in the strength of mages. I also enjoyed that the Fifteen Kingdoms seemed to have a lot of political variation in them, though as other reviewers have pointed out, some of the systems and terms felt anachronistic.<br /><br />I guess that's the primary problem I had with this book: strong concepts, but just not enough explanation to make them fit. Would reading 'president' in a world filled with princes bother me if it had been elaborated upon a lot? Probably not. But when you're already asking me to accept moon and sun magicians, giant flowers that eat people, and some really wonky pacing, well, the background needs to be rock solid and putting a democracy on a continent filled with monarchies doesn't cut it.<br /><br />The other big thing I wanted to mention was pacing. Whee-oo, did I have trouble with the way this book was paced. One page would be a single moment that dragged on far too long, and on the next weeks would skim by. I honestly gave up completely on keeping track of time here, because it was just so erratic and jumpy. Unfortunately, the fact that I had little sense of time also meant that I had little sense of character development.<br /><br />There were a couple of other things that bothered me - use of modern language throughout, some typos which were far worse than I've ever seen in an ARC (including a they're/their confusion), the really strange and rocky development of the romantic relationship between Kerrick and Avry, and a lot of plot points which were never dealt with. I was disappointed that even the main problem of the book wasn't actually <i>resolved</i> at the end, let alone some of the other plot points that had cropped up along the way. To be honest, the book felt too short in a lot of ways - too short to develop its concept properly, too short to wrap up the plot in a tidy fashion, too short to convey the amount of time the characters spent travelling and changing to the readers. Maybe the sequel can fix a lot of these issues, but I won't go out of my way to find it first and see. It's going to take glowing reviews from other people before I return to this series. I will, however, still seek out Poison Study, since Maria V. Snyder has one heck of an imagination.<br /><br /><i>Full disclosure: I recieved a galley copy of this book from the publisher via Netgalley. No external considerations went into this review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14637236589700602340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1023882477" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1023882477" />
    <a title="♛Tash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5451856-tash"><img alt="♛Tash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456286012p2/5451856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1023882477?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♛Tash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♛Tash" href="/user/show/5451856-tash">♛Tash</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/16154900-touch-of-power">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Maria Snyder Die Hard Fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to ♛Tash by: </span>
      Me
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5451856-tash?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1023882477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2766268727209581282">YASSS! I finished it! I really finished it after being tempted to just DNF so many times.<br/><br/>I had a terrific experience reading Snyder's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60510.Poison_Study__Study___1_' title='Poison Study (Study, #1) by Maria V. Snyder' rel='nofollow noopener'>Poison Study</a>. I remember the writing smooth and the world building vivid, so I expected the same thing from Touch of Power, but damn, I was so wrong. In this book, I found Snyder's writing a little amateurish. I had to check the publication dates of the Poison Study and Touch of Power to see which novel came first, and I was surprised to see that Poison Study was </span>
  <span id="freeText2766268727209581282" style="display:none">YASSS! I finished it! I really finished it after being tempted to just DNF so many times.<br><br>I had a terrific experience reading Snyder's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60510.Poison_Study__Study___1_" title="Poison Study (Study, #1) by Maria V. Snyder" rel="nofollow noopener">Poison Study</a>. I remember the writing smooth and the world building vivid, so I expected the same thing from Touch of Power, but damn, I was so wrong. In this book, I found Snyder's writing a little amateurish. I had to check the publication dates of the Poison Study and Touch of Power to see which novel came first, and I was surprised to see that Poison Study was published 4 years before Touch of Power, so I do not understand the decline in quality of Snyder's writing. Her writing was especially unwieldy when describing landscape, fight scenes and even plans, as if she couldn't be bothered to tell us how Avry got to Tohon or how 2 guys can neutralize 6.<br><br>Then we have Avry, sweet, kind, pretty, skilled, brave and selfless Avry. What can she do wrong? Nothing and that is my problem with her character. I know she's a healer and that she feels the need to heal everyone sick and is even willing to die for her calling, but shouldn't the human instinct to survive override the sacrifices of her calling? Maybe I am just a selfish little shit and obvs not a heroine, so Avry didn't connect to me at all. Kerrick - I found quite meh. He's a prince and a forest mage, and starts out as a despotic leader of a group in a mission to find a healer but grows softer as the story progresses to the point he says things like "And you broke through the ice around my heart..." <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434121947ra/15176708.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yup. <br><br>Then we have Tohon the all powerful life mage/necromancer, of course, he had to be handsome with a killer smile too, and a Daddy never loved me complex. In the book he tells Avry why he hates Kerrick. I'll skip the specifics, but damn, that was lame, so lame I screamed at my Kindle to grow the fuck up because high school angst should be left in high school! #intensityintensifies<br><br>I honestly think that the story will progress in the following books in the series, but, for now, I am done with this series. <br><br>*fin*</span>
  <a data-text-id="2766268727209581282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer10912743356194628746">What can I say about this story? I fell in love with all of it. It's epic!! It has it all, adventure, comradeship, romance, betrayal, friendship, loss, magic, sacrifice, evil, set in an amazing fantasy world.<br/><br/>Avry is an amazing character, a heroine so strong, so compationate, so loyal, it was marvelous being in her head. <br/><br/>Snyder weaves an interesting, very complicated fantasy world, similar to the one in her "Study" series. All the characters are very well developed, from the minor ones to the vil</span>
  <span id="freeText10912743356194628746" style="display:none">What can I say about this story? I fell in love with all of it. It's epic!! It has it all, adventure, comradeship, romance, betrayal, friendship, loss, magic, sacrifice, evil, set in an amazing fantasy world.<br><br>Avry is an amazing character, a heroine so strong, so compationate, so loyal, it was marvelous being in her head. <br><br>Snyder weaves an interesting, very complicated fantasy world, similar to the one in her "Study" series. All the characters are very well developed, from the minor ones to the villains, to the ones that form her family in the end. <br><br>And of course Kerrick. If you like your heroes brooding, grumpy, not giving the heroine the time of day, then you're in for a treat with Kerrick. First he hits her. Then he ties her in a tree, without food or cloak, every night. Then he insists she gives her life for his friend. Wouldn't you fall in love with a "charming" man like him?<br><br>But you just can't help but fall in love with him, just like Avry did.<br><br>I wonder where their journey will lead them next and I'm most curious to find out all this mystery surrounding the lilies. Who would have thought that these plants would be so intriguing, they have me speculating all kinds of senarios about their involvement with the plague and the healers and.... I just can't imagine what?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1510038988i/24380519.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1206281968" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1206281968" />
    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1206281968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12512273020547897841">When I say that I was going into <i>Touch of Power </i> with astronomical expectations I wouldn't be exaggerating. I hope that the next books will be even better, but this one was great. Enjoyable, captivating read. My only problem was, that I had too much expectations after reading <i>Poison Study</i> series.<br/><br/>The first half of this book was rather slow-paced, the characters were constantly walking somewhere through the woods and I was slightly bored at first. But halfway through the book, the story finally pi</span>
  <span id="freeText12512273020547897841" style="display:none">When I say that I was going into <i>Touch of Power </i> with astronomical expectations I wouldn't be exaggerating. I hope that the next books will be even better, but this one was great. Enjoyable, captivating read. My only problem was, that I had too much expectations after reading <i>Poison Study</i> series.<br><br>The first half of this book was rather slow-paced, the characters were constantly walking somewhere through the woods and I was slightly bored at first. But halfway through the book, the story finally picked up and interesting things started to happen! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446748078i/16889646.jpg" width="390" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The characters were great. <s>Well, most of them.</s><br><br><b>Avry </b> was kind and selfless heroine and at first, I expected her to be one of those 'damsels in distress'. But she very much surprised me with her strength, stubbornness and spirit!<br><br><b>“Sorry. An overdeveloped nurturing instinct comes with being a healer.”</b><br><br><b>Belen 'Alias: The Poppa Bear'</b> was definitely my favourite character. Big guy with even bigger heart! He was sweet, caring and protective of his little group of friends.<br><br><b>“When we reached the door, Belen stepped in the way. 'If any harm—'<br>'Comes to her, you’ll rip out my arms. Got it,' Kerrick said.<br>'I’m serious,' Belen said.<br>'I know. Do you really think I’d put her in danger?'<br>'Not on purpose, but things happen that are out of your control.'<br>Kerrick gave him a tight smile. 'You mean I'm not omnipotent?'<br>'You're not even semi-potent.'<br>'Is that even a word?' Kerrick asked.<br>'He probably means you're impotent,' I offered.”</b><br><br><b>Kerrick.</b> When I say that I didn't like him at first, it would be an understatement. When we meet him in the first chapters, he's definitely not likable character. But I had in mind, that he's not supposed to be likable and that there's something behind his behavior. But through this book, you can see very slow character development on his part. And at the end I understood his actions and even started to like him. Maybe he'll impress in the next book!<br><br><b>“No. I took this job in self-defense. Quain burns everything. Belen thinks jerky is all we need to survive. Flea's idea of a good meal is something that hasn't been in a garbage can first. And Kerrick poisoned us-”<br>“Not on purpose,” Kerrick said. “The meat looked done.”</b><br><br><b>Loren and Quain 'Alias: The Monkeys'</b> were funny little duo. Sometimes I tend to confuse these two, because they seemed almost the same.<br><br><b>“Thinking of learning the assassin arts, Belen?” Loren asked.<br>“Isn’t that a rare flower? Maybe he wants to get into gardening. I hear that’s what older people do when they reach their dotage,” Quain teased.<br>Belen shook his head. “Two brains and not a bit of intelligence between them. Good thing the monkeys are entertaining or I’d have left them back in Ryazan.”</b><br><br><b>Flea</b> lived most of his life in the streets. He's funny and curious boy, but also young survivor wise beyond his age.<br><br><b>“Flea stared at us, "I can't decide what's worse. Losing family members or not having a family member to lose.” </b><br><br>And at last the villain of this story - <b>Tohan</b>. Twisted, jealous and psychotic maniac with daddy issues.<br><br><b>“Yes. Living things do well under my care.” He gave me a wry smile, acknowledging the irony. “As long as I care about them.” Then he sobered. “People, on the other hand, are not worth caring for.”</b><br><br>I kind of liked him and definitely need to know what problems will he cause in the next book - <i>Scent of Magic</i>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12512273020547897841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer718737277906194031">So I enjoyed this book, but didn't LOVE it. Poison Study (by this author) is one of my ALL TIME FAVES so I can't help compare all her other heroines to that one, and no one ever lives up to her 100%. I enjoyed the magic worldbuilding, for some reason I just felt one step ahead of the characters frequently. I didn't 100% feel the attraction between the two main characters either, so maybe that made me a bit less invested. I enjoyed the heroine's POV though, and am interested to see the second in </span>
  <span id="freeText718737277906194031" style="display:none">So I enjoyed this book, but didn't LOVE it. Poison Study (by this author) is one of my ALL TIME FAVES so I can't help compare all her other heroines to that one, and no one ever lives up to her 100%. I enjoyed the magic worldbuilding, for some reason I just felt one step ahead of the characters frequently. I didn't 100% feel the attraction between the two main characters either, so maybe that made me a bit less invested. I enjoyed the heroine's POV though, and am interested to see the second in the series. Felt a bit young adult-ish in tone, so it would be good for teen readers.</span>

<div id="review_209698277" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/209698277" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3060045-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350249427p2/3060045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/209698277?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/3060045-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer209698277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer738880382579264339">This review is for an ARC kindly given to me by the Amazon Vine UK Review program.<br/><br/>Touch of Power is Poison Study good!!! *HUGE CHEER* I haven't enjoyed a book by Maria V Snyder so much in a long time (even though they are usually great); I stayed up reading til all hours and was even late to work because I couldn't put it down! I really hope you agree with me when you get a chance to read it. I would definitely recommend this as required reading for Maria fans ASAP!! <br/><br/>I really liked Maria's new h</span>
  <span id="freeText738880382579264339" style="display:none">This review is for an ARC kindly given to me by the Amazon Vine UK Review program.<br /><br />Touch of Power is Poison Study good!!! *HUGE CHEER* I haven't enjoyed a book by Maria V Snyder so much in a long time (even though they are usually great); I stayed up reading til all hours and was even late to work because I couldn't put it down! I really hope you agree with me when you get a chance to read it. I would definitely recommend this as required reading for Maria fans ASAP!! <br /><br />I really liked Maria's new heroine, Avry. She is fierce and stubborn, but also kind and brave. I liked her so much more than Opal from the Glass trilogy. She is as engaging as Yelena from Poison Study without being too much like her... both characters share similarities, but they are not one and the same. Avry is a healer, who can take peoples' illnesses from them as a cure, but she must suffer the illness herself. Fortunately she has an advanced speed of healing, or she'd never get anything done! <br /><br />The story picks up in the aftermath of a devastating plague, which the healers guild were unable to cure without dying themselves. As a result, healers are not revered by society, but rather they are hunted drifters. Avry finds herself incarcerated, awaiting death, but then is rescued by a motley crew who want her to heal their leader, Ryne, who lies in suspended animation in a magical coma in a distant land. He has a bad reputation, and he has the plague; healing him would kill Avry. <br /><br />The gang (Kerrick, Belen, Vinn, Quain and Flea) do their best to convince Avry, through any method possible, that she should heal Ryne as they believe he is the only person who can bring all the shreds of their plague-ridden kingdom together and restore order. There are several other potential leaders who disagree though, and they all make a play for Avry to varying success. One develops into a wonderful villain, who just made my skin crawl! (Excellent work Maria!!)<br /><br />Avry travels with the gang for most of the book, and there is a really beautiful camaraderie which grows between them, after some testing times... of course there is a love interest, and the development of that aspect was simply delicious to read. When there was finally some kissing, I was in seventh heaven!! <br /><br />What I really enjoy about Maria's writing, as a whole, is that she creates characters with believable skills. I know she often learns these skills herself, and this time I really enjoyed reading about juggling and knife throwing! Magic is also woven very carefully through the seams of the book; no one is all powerful, but some people have really interesting talents. I also love how rich her characters are; I really feel like I know Avry, Belen, Kerrick, and Flea. <br /><br />I was initially completely baffled by the bizarre mention of the peace and death lilies, giant plants which can consume a man whole, but actually it all made sense in the end, and I am totally gutted that I have to wait for the story to continue!! This has all the makings of a really wonderful fantasy trilogy... now... how long do I have to wait for the next one?! <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="738880382579264339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_235375480" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/235375480" />
    <a title="Bird" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1614841-bird"><img alt="Bird" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241745174p2/1614841.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235375480?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bird" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bird" href="/user/show/1614841-bird">Bird</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1614841-bird?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi">fantasy-and-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1614841-bird?shelf=first-in-a-series">first-in-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1614841-bird?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1614841-bird?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235375480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4564830011447113968">I loved Snyder's first book, Poison Study, and since then I've been a faithful reader of everything she's written. I haven't actually enjoyed any of her books as much as PS, and I think I keep reading in hopes of discovering another book like that one. Alas, her most recent effort doesn't come close to PS for me.<br/><br/>Snyder creates the kind of fantasy world I love, which has a nice medieval flavor. Snyder's never been one to info-dump in her stories, which I appreciate, but in this story I felt like </span>
  <span id="freeText4564830011447113968" style="display:none">I loved Snyder's first book, Poison Study, and since then I've been a faithful reader of everything she's written. I haven't actually enjoyed any of her books as much as PS, and I think I keep reading in hopes of discovering another book like that one. Alas, her most recent effort doesn't come close to PS for me.<br /><br />Snyder creates the kind of fantasy world I love, which has a nice medieval flavor. Snyder's never been one to info-dump in her stories, which I appreciate, but in this story I felt like the world-building information was doled out in small pieces in such a haphazard function that I spent much of the story feeling like I didn't truly understand the world she had created.<br /><br />The story is set up in a "quest" format, with the book centered around a journey from one place to another in order to achieve some aim. It's never been my favorite storytelling device, maybe because it can tend toward monotony. (They traveled. They ran into some trouble. They traveled some more.)<br /><br />The group of men Avry travels with are basically stereotypes (one young jokester who wants to be taken seriously, the hulking "teddy-bear" protector, the ruthless leader), and never felt fully fleshed-out to me. Avry herself feels boring to me, and even when she tries to do something heroic it ends up seeming halfhearted. She wasn't as strong as I like my heroines to be, although that may change in the next two books.<br /><br />My main problem with the story, however, lies in the budding romance that develops. Now, I love romance. I'll generally only read fantasy if there's some romantic element to keep my attention. But Snyder has failed to give me a hero I can root for. (The spoiler below is only really "spoiler-y" in that it reveals who the love interest is, which isn't apparent right away. At least not to me anyway, since I guessed incorrectly at first.) <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A man who hits a woman in the beginning of the book CANNOT later become that woman's love interest. It just can't happen. Kerrick's behavior is inexcusable, I don't care how Snyder tries to explain it away. He's under stress, he's scared, he didn't mean it, blah, blah. It is NEVER alright for a man to strike a woman, and it certainly shouldn't happen between future lovers. How can I root for a hero who might hurt the heroine the next time he gets "stressed"? This is the second time Snyder has written about this type of romance, and I'm tired of it. (Readers of her Glass trilogy will remember that Opal is kidnapped and tortured by Devlin, who, by the end of the third book, has become her lover. But don't worry folks, it's OK because he was under the influence of magical blood at the time. You know, blood he chose to consume in his quest for power.) It really bothers me that Snyder excuses violence toward women so easily. In all honesty, it may cause me to stop reading her novels. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I don't know if I'll continue on with the series, or even seek out future books by this author. I've been disappointed by this author more than once, and the "romance" in this one left me feeling cold. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4564830011447113968" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2429635271939019139">Did I just enjoy this as much as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60510.Poison_Study__Study___1_' title='Poison Study (Study, #1) by Maria V. Snyder' rel='nofollow noopener'>Poison Study</a>? I guess I did. WOW. Maria V. Snyder knows how to tell stories. I've been reading her books for a while now and they all are so good. I was a little hesitant toward this because..it wasn't in the Poison Study universe. It is a completely different story set in a different world with a different type of magic. <b>AND I LOVED IT A LOT.</b><br/><br/>The story follows Avry, a girl with the power of healing. She can cure almost anyone no matter what sickness or injuries t</span>
  <span id="freeText2429635271939019139" style="display:none">Did I just enjoy this as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60510.Poison_Study__Study___1_" title="Poison Study (Study, #1) by Maria V. Snyder" rel="nofollow noopener">Poison Study</a>? I guess I did. WOW. Maria V. Snyder knows how to tell stories. I've been reading her books for a while now and they all are so good. I was a little hesitant toward this because..it wasn't in the Poison Study universe. It is a completely different story set in a different world with a different type of magic. <b>AND I LOVED IT A LOT.</b><br /><br />The story follows Avry, a girl with the power of healing. She can cure almost anyone no matter what sickness or injuries they might have. But in this world, healers are persecuted because of their abilities and are killed at sight. Why? because they are blamed for a plague that killed a lot of people. SO Avry has been hiding for three years until one day she is rescued by a man named Kerrick and his group of comrades and he wants her to heal a person who's very important to him. The story itself takes place in a country that's about to have a civil war because there are a lot of noble people that seek total control over it. <br /><br />Once again, Maria V. Snyder tells a story that is heavily on politics, with amazing characters and a subtle and slow hate-to-love romance that is amazing.** <br /><br />**There were one thing that I didn't like at all and it was that in the very beginning when Avry and Kerrick started their journey together they had a fight and he slaps her. <u>No, I'm not making excuses for him, and no, I don't approve of his behaviour at that moment, but at least he made amends to her after it</u>. I wish that scene wasn't in the book, because it was for the solely purpose of showing that the two of them hated each other at first. But that "hate" between those characters could've develop differently. That moment ruined the start of the book for me, but I had faith in the author so I kept reading. The relationship was amazing at the end, and Kerrick shows a great character development, but I still feel obligated to acknowledge that moment, because after all, he's the love interest of the story. It surprised me a lot because in her other series the author built such a healthy relationship so I don't understand why she wrote that scene in this book at the beginning.</span>

<div id="review_280055538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280055538" />
    <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt"><img alt="Jacob Proffitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280055538?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Proffitt" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/13509158-touch-of-power">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280055538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15246924417988355953">I enjoyed ¾ of this story. The setup was fascinating. A plague has recently finished wiping out a substantial portion of the population so there is a lot of civil upheaval as people figure out how to get by on a fraction of the resources they need to support the prior social (and commercial) infrastructure. The book doesn't put it in those terms anywhere, but it's clear that Snyder has thought through the implications and complications of such an event and the actions of the people are completel</span>
  <span id="freeText15246924417988355953" style="display:none">I enjoyed ¾ of this story. The setup was fascinating. A plague has recently finished wiping out a substantial portion of the population so there is a lot of civil upheaval as people figure out how to get by on a fraction of the resources they need to support the prior social (and commercial) infrastructure. The book doesn't put it in those terms anywhere, but it's clear that Snyder has thought through the implications and complications of such an event and the actions of the people are completely plausible given their situation—including their hatred and persecution of the healers who failed to save them from the one disease it turns out they couldn't fight.<br /> <br />Avry appears to be the last healer and is on the run. When she is captured by a band of men looking for her special talent, she finds herself in a completely untenable position. She deals with it as best she can, getting to know her captors in the process. These friendships are dynamic, though enough simplified to earn my designation of Young Adult. The leader of the band, Kerrick, remains unsympathetic (to Avry, readers have enough distance to discern his motives much sooner than Avry can), though, putting the whole band in a tough spot—do they support Avry or Kerrick as it becomes clear that neither alone has the solution to the problems they face?<br /><br />I really enjoyed this part of the story, even though it was pretty obvious that Avry suffered from unfounded assumptions that kept her stupid way longer than was really justified. There were enough events that ran counter to her assumptions that she really <em>should</em> have asked clarifying questions at a couple of points and simply didn't for no apparent reason. It's not like she was playing shy or didn't demand answers to awkward questions at pretty much the drop of a hat all the time, anyway. It was really out of character.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the last quarter of the book (or so) was an egregious example of authorial manipulation. It's the last bit of the book, so this is going to have to be tagged as a spoiler. Unspoilery summary: the villain is an evil, mustache-twirling fiend except that he somehow isn't, probably because the author didn't want to deal with the obvious consequences if he actually were. Only he really is. Only not. You see the problem...<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[We learn about Tohan from second hand throughout the novel. His actions are obviously selfish and evil (absent some mitigating explanation that turns out not to exist). Then we meet him and Avry allows herself to be captured by the would-be king of the world. Bear in mind that she has had, at that point, multiple witnesses from those who know him relatively intimately who confirm that he is selfish and abusive and likely outright evil. Bear in mind, too, that she knows that he enjoys using (and abusing) women in his power games with others, including, notably Kerrick. And she even knows that his magic is all about manipulating emotions and that he has no internal or moral limitations on his use of that magic to get whatever he wants. And yet knowing all that, Avry still delivers herself into his power.<br /><br />This is beyond stupid. Avry at that point has more or less signed up for rape and torture. Her friends warn her, though obliquely, that this is a bad idea. And it turns out that Tohan <em>is</em> every bit as abusive as was hinted at by others. He is capricious and selfish and doesn't have any problem manipulating, even outright abusing, others to get exactly what he wants. And it is clear that he wants Avry sexually in addition to wanting to use her healing powers for his own purposes. And yet, for no reason whatsoever, he limits his intrusions to a couple of kisses and forcing her (through magically applied pain) to wear a dress that is more revealing than Avry is comfortable with. She is his captive for near a month, at least some of that time in disgrace and being punished. Yet all Avry suffers is a grimy dungeon and some unwanted passionate kisses. I'm sorry, but Snyder completely lost me here. If you don't want the burden of a heroine (and story) dealing with rape, then don't have Avry so capricious about whose power she willingly enters. Or have the villain have <em>some</em> realistic reason for avoiding it (he's gay? asexual? satisfied with his current partner? Not completely selfish and evil? Any of these would do). But no, Snyder doesn't justify it at all. It's like her villain is evil, selfish, and capricious, but somehow never actually carries his “seduction” to its natural and obvious conclusion, even when he’s near halfway there, already.<br /><br />This whole section of the novel, I felt the burden of waiting for the obviously impending rape only for it not to ever happen. That's a large emotional burden that needed <em>some</em> justification or relief. At that point, it feels like physical and sexual abuse is a toy that Snyder includes for titillation rather than as something her characters might actually experience. That kind of capricious manipulation cheapens actual instances of rape and abuse because real people don't have a benevolent author watching their back and preventing the bad guys from going too far.<br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>That last problem with the story completely broke immersion for me and fundamentally broke my willingness to engage with the story. However much I might like Avry and the details of a world decimated by plague, I'm just not interested in a world so casually and obviously manipulated by the author. I'm deeply disappointed in Snyder whose works I generally otherwise enjoy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15246924417988355953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NxuTtoyMJqxy5h22Cu2jGBoJU7v0rPxHwa1609J0FMTfN72mu8k80pbELiTFEnKDeMG/p8GIi6VXFFqcRZtlZA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6297957092928646103">When Maria V. Snyder was younger, she aspired to be a storm chaser in the American Midwest so she attended Pennsylvania State University and earned a Bachelor of Science degree in Meteorology. Much to her chagrin, forecasting the weather wasn’t in her skill set so she spent a number of years as an environmental meteorologist, which is not exciting...at all. Bored at work and needing a creative out</span>
  <span id="freeText6297957092928646103" style="display:none">When Maria V. Snyder was younger, she aspired to be a storm chaser in the American Midwest so she attended Pennsylvania State University and earned a Bachelor of Science degree in Meteorology. Much to her chagrin, forecasting the weather wasn’t in her skill set so she spent a number of years as an environmental meteorologist, which is not exciting...at all. Bored at work and needing a creative outlet, she started writing fantasy and science fiction stories. Over twenty novels and numerous short stories later, Maria’s learned a thing or three about writing. She’s been on the New York Times bestseller list, won a dozen awards, and has earned her Masters of Arts degree in Writing from Seton Hill University, where she is now a faculty member. Her favorite color is red. She loves dogs, but is allergic, instead she has a big black tom cat named…Kitty (apparently naming cats isn’t in her skill set either). Maria also has a husband and two children who are an inspiration for her writing when they aren't being a distraction. Note: She mentions her cat before her family. <br /><br />When she's not writing she's either playing volleyball, traveling, or taking pictures. Being a writer, though is a ton of fun. Where else can you take fencing lessons, learn how to ride a horse, study marital arts, learn how to pick a lock, take glass blowing classes and attend Astronomy Camp and call it research? Maria will be the first one to tell you it's not working as a meteorologist.<br /><br />Readers are welcome to check out her website for book excerpts, free short stories, maps, blog, and her schedule at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.MariaVSnyder.com">http://www.MariaVSnyder.com</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6297957092928646103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
